<rating>5< /rating>< Review>
The sign outside says $5 large pizza 1 topping! You have to wait 20 minutes otherwise you get a slice for $5. We ordered two pizzas and waited outside in the patio. They were delicious and worth the wait. There's a big oak tree adjacent to the parking lot with a picnic bench that's even more pleasant. And there's a water spigot  so you can walk and water your dog .  Space to park and turn around an RV . They have a wide selection of Wine Liquor and sandwiches and we met a couple of locals. Locals know where it's at! Staff was pleasant and helpful. Maybe they can tidy up the bathroom a little bit. Overall a positive experience.</Review>

<user>109567731266535439057</user>< text>
The only thing shiftier than a rental car is this co-branded Avis/Budget franchisee. Arrived at the 7:30 am opening time to pick up the car I reserved online for $70/weekend. The printed contract stated $130. When asked about the discrepancy the owner said 'it's $60 for the extra 30 minutes beyond three days'.  Huh? By now it's 7:40 am. Turns out the following Monday is a holiday and they don't open until 8 am. Since I "can't return (the car) until 8 am, it's an extra $60 'late fee'".

OK-I'll wait 20 minutes, rent the car today at 8:00 am and thus stay within the three day window. "Too late," he quips, "the transaction is complete and your credit card's been charged!"  When I challenged his lack of a signed rental agreement he countered "all I can do now is void your existing reservation and book a new one" -at a substantially higher price. No thanks. As I walked out he magically gained the ability to credit my previously 'unchangeable' 7:30 am "transaction" $60-but only after I returned the car, and (naturally) with nothing confirmed in writing.

Righhhht.  Read the other reviews for how these shady undocumented future 'promises' have played out. I can only imagine the return damage inspection.

Walked across the street, hopped in a Gig-car, drove where I needed to go and conveniently "returned" it right in front of my own house. No slight-of-contract shenanigans, trumped-up damages or belligerent business owners necessary-and with the fuel included Gig turned out to be cheaper!

UPDATE:  Adding insult to injury, the response from "socialinfo@Avis" was just empty-Google-review-fixing.  Never heard a peep back.  Nice work, Avis.</text>

I don't know how to put this any other way, but this is one of the most special places I have ever been too.  This might seem a little extreme for a tea shop; however, Sophie's Cuppa Tea is a sanctuary of peace and serenity.  The owners, Bei and John, are two of the most incredible people I have ever met and they also serve the best tea I have ever had.  I can promise everyone that they will not be disappointed if they come to this shop.   In addition to the shop, if you are looking for your next vacation, ask them about their yearly China Tea Trip. <review>Stepping through the door of this beautifully curated spot in Montclair, is essentially stepping into another world, a world of beautiful art, rare porcelain, and even finer teas.
Lovingly tended by John and Sophie,  Tea masters, who have a deep knowledge tea based on regular travel to Fujian as well as other ancient tea sources in China, I was treated to simply the best large glass of simply Wu Long, (Their spelling, I have no knowledge whatsoever of Mandarin) that I've ever had, and was also treated to a rare sight. I have seen tea wheels but none larger than the one I was presented with At Cuppa Tea, easily 30 inches in diameter,, with a specially made tea wheel stand you will only find here, because they had it made especially for their tea wheels.
The decor and mood in the place was an absolute oasis of calm and tranquility in a ever-maddening world, (Even in Montclair)  and is now on my to-do list every time I am in the neighborhood.
I'd try the Wu Long, however, their green tea selection, ( I am a Jasmine pearl fanatic) is simply a marvel of tea curation, and John, was a gracious and knowledgeable host,  with an affable manner sometimes missing in high level tea establishments, and I ended up leaving with a rare Jasmine, as well as a vastly improved attitude, as will you when you visit John and Sophie's Cuppa Tea in Montclair.  Treat yourself to some relaxation!</review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNgDHgtqvy_WVmEuebPcTnsnaCRPnQLMPEGw7YJ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPH-uaCFduSffXEZEpQBOtSIQT1kkDJ_f6z3IXa=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< Response>

< Review>
A real gem. Sophie's is more than a place to enjoy a cuppa tea. It's an experience and a community where everyone's welcome. It's like a favorite local pub, but instead of pints and salty snacks, it's rare Chinese teas and delicious pastries. The owners' Saturday tastings and talks reveal the immense world of Chinese teas. John and Bei source their teas by traveling to China so they're deeply knowledgeable, passionate, and a joy to talk with. If you have an interest in learning about tea, or just want a great place to rest and read, you should stop in.<//Review>

< user_id>
108824308973432510135</user_id>
<username>j. rodman< /username><time>1480204973861</time>< Rating>
3</Rating>
< Text>
Tea selection and quality are good, far above what you'd get at a Peet's etc.  However, I wasn't amazed with my wulong, having had better experiences at e.g. Imperial Tea Court or ordering from Red Blossom.  Perhaps the comparison is unfair, and it's certainly the best tea you'll find in a walk-in store for at least a 6-mile radius.

Presentation is a little westernized receiving the brewed tea in a mug with no possibility to experience the progression of flavor as a gaiwan would offer.

The real downside though is the noise.  It was impossible to focus on my tea with a ridiculous conversation going on a few feet away.  By comparison, Peet's down at Lakeshore has a moderate hubbub going on at times, but is far easier to ignore and read, or participate if so inclined. I'm not sure if this could be solved with decor / sound-muting panelling or similar.

Unfortunately the overall verdict is it's not worth the trip just to buy tea to take home when there are so many other high quality options in Berkeley & San Francisco, and it's not a pleasant environment to spend time in contemplation or reading unless at an unpopular time.  If I lived in the neighborhood I might make it a habit.<//Text>

I recently went to Evans Vista to get an oil change for my wife's car. Normally I go to San Marcos, but I was at my parent's house in Carlsbad and Vista was closer.

I cannot say I will ever go back to Evans Vista.

1) At Evan's San Marcos, my oil change out the door price is usually around $48 after coupon. At Evan's Vista, the price seemed a little high, but I did not have my old paperwork with me to remind me how much I usually pay. Upon my being able to check my previous service receipts, I was normally charged ~$48 (going back to 2017) for synthetic oil changes at Evan's San Marcos (after discount), and at Evan's Vista, they charged me $74 out the door (after discount). I do not know what was different (Per the receipt, Valvoline Oil Syn Oil was different), but I felt a little cheated at the price charged post discount at Evan's Vista (especially since PepBoys across the street was $75 -$20 web discount for a synthetic oil change). This was not a deal-breaker, because I should have been more prepared and questioned the high quote, but it was disappointing for me. In the future, I am going to call ahead and get an "out-the-door" quote. (minus one star)

2) I was called and told that my shocks/struts were overdue and bad. Evan's Vista told me my tires showed signs of cupping, my shocks/struts were bad, and that one of the rear shocks/struts were leaking. I told Evan's Vista I had my shocks/struts replaced less than 30k miles ago at a different repair shop and that they should not be showing much wear. They stuck with their story, even when I went to pick the car up they confirmed the story for the third time and "verified" with the mechanic. I took my car to PepBoys to get my shocks/struts inspected (at a $20 fee). PepBoys said they found no signs of cupping on the tires and all my shocks/struts were healthy (no signs of leakage either). This is too much for me. I need to be able to trust my mechanic to not upsell me something I do not need. (minus four stars)

For a routine oil change @ ~$48, I paid $26 more than normal for an oil change + $20 to get a second opinion on my shocks/struts. $46 extra dollars total for 'routine service', and suspicious recommendation to replace my 'newer' shocks/struts makes me lose trust in this location.< /text>
